<DOCNO>1808</DOCNO>
<NameOfSubstance>Dimethicone</NameOfSubstance>
<CASRegistryNumber>9006-65-9</CASRegistryNumber>
<unii>92RU3N3Y1O</unii>
<htox>/HUMAN EXPOSURE STUDIES/ A randomized crossover study of the effects of dimethicone (dimeticone) on the pharmacokinetics and pharmacodynamics of ethyl biscoumacetate was conducted in 6 healthy subjects (ages 22-28 yr) who received a dose of 300 mg ethyl biscoumacetate (Tromexane) alone or with 2.25 g dimethicone (Gel de Polysilane Midy). The peak concentration of ethyl biscoumacetate was 40.3 mg/L when given alone and 31 mg/L in the presence of dimethicone. No significant changes in other pharmacokinetic and pharmacodynamic parameters were observed. It was concluded that dimethicone causes a slight increase in the bioavailability of ethyl biscoumacetate.[Copie X; Therapie 48 (13): 119-123 (1993) http://toxnet.nlm.nih.gov/cgi-bin/sis/search2/r?dbs+toxline:@term+@DOCNO+IPA/93/1036161] **PEER REVIEWED** </htox>
<intc>A randomized crossover study of the effects of dimethicone (dimeticone) on the pharmacokinetics and pharmacodynamics of ethyl biscoumacetate was conducted in 6 healthy subjects (ages 22-28 yr) who received a dose of 300 mg ethyl biscoumacetate (Tromexane) alone or with 2.25 g dimethicone (Gel de Polysilane Midy). The peak concentration of ethyl biscoumacetate was 40.3 mg/L when given alone and 31 mg/L in the presence of dimethicone. No significant changes in other pharmacokinetic and pharmacodynamic parameters were observed. It was concluded that dimethicone causes a slight increase in the bioavailability of ethyl biscoumacetate.[Copie X; Therapie 48 (13): 119-123 (1993) http://toxnet.nlm.nih.gov/cgi-bin/sis/search2/r?dbs+toxline:@term+@DOCNO+IPA/93/1036161] **PEER REVIEWED** </intc>

<htox>/HUMAN EXPOSURE STUDIES/ The efficacy of liquid antacid containing 600 mg aluminum hydroxide (I) and 300 mg magnesium hydroxide (II)/5 mL was compared to that of antacid tablet containing 400 mg I, 400 mg II and 30 mg simethicone by measuring intragastric pH in 23 healthy subjects in both the fasted and postprandial state, following the administration of one or 2 tablets, 5 or 10 ml of the liquid antacid, or placebo in a randomized, crossover, placebo-controlled study. One tablet and 5 ml liquid yielded similar results in fasting subjects, with mean peak pH values of 5.2 and 4.8, and durations above pH 3.5 of 25 and 40 min, respectively. Doubling the dose to 10 ml of liquid and 2 tablets produced a peak pH of 6.7 and 4.8, and maintained above pH 3.5 for 40 and 15 min, respectively. In the fed subjects, neither antacid formulation at either dose significantly raised the intragastric pH. No adverse reactions were reported throughout the studies. It was concluded that further studies are needed to establish the optimal time for postprandial administration of antacids.[Thomson AB et al; Clin. Ther 10 (2): 158-168 (1988) http://toxnet.nlm.nih.gov/cgi-bin/sis/search2/r?dbs+toxline:@term+@DOCNO+IPA/89/852058] **PEER REVIEWED** </htox>
<htox>/HUMAN EXPOSURE STUDIES/ The effectiveness, costs and side effects of a conventional pancrelipase (Cotazym; I) were compared alone and with Maalox Plus (aluminum hydroxide in combination with magnesium hydroxide, simethicone) or with bile salts (Cotazym-65-B), and with the new coated preparation (Pancrease; II) in 11 children aged 8 to 18 yr with cystic fibrosis. All patients were given the following regimens for one week: (1) I, 6 capsules with meals, 2 with snacks; (2) I, 6 capsules plus 30 ml of Maalox Plus, given simultaneously at mealtime, 2 capsules with 15 ml of the antacid with snacks; (3) Cotazym-65-B, 6 capsules with meals, 2 with snacks; (4) II, 3 capsules with meals, one with snacks. The results showed that caloric intake did not differ significantly among the regimens. II was associated with somewhat less stool mass, but little difference was observed in stool frequency. Mean values for nitrogen excretion during I with Maalox Plus and alone were similar, but differed by a small though significant degree from those obtained during II and Cotazym-65-B administration. Although normal fat absorption was not seen in any patient during any of the enzyme regimens, steatorrhea was significantly less during treatment with I and Maalox Plus and with II. Improved fat absorption was seen in 9 of 11 patients when Maalox Plus was added to I. Uric acid excretion averaged 657 mg/day, which is higher than normal mean values of 300 to 400 mg/day. One patient had an elevated serum uric acid concentration (10 mg/dL) during all 4 regimens. The cost of II was the lowest of the 4 regimens. Although the individual cost for I was less, the lower required number of capsules of II reduced the cost of treatment. Maalox Plus required to improve fat absorption further increased the cost, and generally was not liked by the patients. It was concluded that among 4 treatment regimens studied, II appears to be the preferred treatment for pancreatic enzyme replacement in cystic fibrosis. None of the pancreatic enzyme supplements used, however, alone or with the addition of bile salts, Maalox Plus, or enteric coating, completely corrected the malabsorption of fat.[Nassif EG et al; J Pediatr 98(ref 14): 320-323 (1981) http://toxnet.nlm.nih.gov/cgi-bin/sis/search2/r?dbs+toxline:@term+@DOCNO+IPA/82/432073] **PEER REVIEWED** </htox>
<htox>/CASE REPORTS/ Two cases of pulmonary aspiration of gastric contents following administration of aluminum hydroxide, 40 mg/mL, magnesium hydroxide, 40 mg/mL, simethicone, 4 mg/mL (Mylanta; I) during grand mal seizures which occurred during delivery are reported. Each patient had received 15 mL of I, and the pH of the gastric aspirate was above 3. Each patient recovered without any clinical or laboratory evidence of pulmonary abnormality. It was suggested that routine administration of antacids to parturients during labor should be continued.[Bassell GM, Gatha MH; Anesthesiology 52 (ref 7): 450-451 (1980) http://toxnet.nlm.nih.gov/cgi-bin/sis/search2/r?dbs+toxline:@term+@DOCNO+IPA/80/405027] **PEER REVIEWED** </htox>
<htox>/CASE REPORTS/ Apnea in a 5-wk-old infant who received Ovol, a combination of dicyclomine hydrochloride and simethicone, was reported.[Spoudeas H, Shribman S; Br Med J 288: 1230 (1984) http://toxnet.nlm.nih.gov/cgi-bin/sis/search2/r?dbs+toxline:@term+@DOCNO+IPA/85/610038] **PEER REVIEWED** </htox>
<htox>/CASE REPORTS/ The case of a 4-wk-old infant who received an accidental overdose of Piptalin suspension containing 4 mg of pipenzolate bromide and 40 mg of simethicone per 5 mL as therapy for infant colic is reported. The dose prescribed for the child was 5 mL of an 80% dilution of the suspension before feedings. The child was being breast fed 10-12 times a day, resulting in a total daily dose 3 times greater than the manufacturer's recommended daily dose. After the eighth dose, the mother noted that the infant was difficult to rouse. It is noted that the data sheet for Piptalin is under revision to read "2.5 mL 15 min before each feed up to a maximum of 4 times daily" for infants under 10 kg.[Sadler EB; Pharm J 240: 768 (1988) http://toxnet.nlm.nih.gov/cgi-bin/sis/search2/r?dbs+toxline:@term+@DOCNO+IPA/89/842222] **PEER REVIEWED** </htox>
<ntox>/LABORATORY ANIMALS: Developmental or Reproductive Toxicity/ Dow Corning Antifoam A /(simethicone)/ compound, a food grade polydimethylsiloxane was evaluated for its developmental toxicity potential in New Zealand White rabbits. Time-mated female rabbits were fed Antifoam A compound in the diet at concentrations of 0, 0.5, 1.0, and 2.5% from the morning of day 6 through the morning of day 19 of gestation. Clinical signs of toxicity in the females were monitored daily during treatment. At termination (gd 29), confirmed-pregnant females (20-22 per group) were evaluated for gestational outcome; each live fetus was examined for external, visceral and skeletal malformations. There were no overt signs of toxicity in the dams, and no statistically significant differences in food consumption were observed between treated and control rabbits. No adverse effects were noted in mean maternal body weight or liver weight. The incidence of resorptions among the total fetal population was not altered by feeding Antifoam A compound. Male and female pup weights were not affected by the maternal treatment. There were no significant treatment related adverse effects in the incidence of external, visceral or skeletal abnormalities. In summary, oral administration of food grade polydimethylsiloxane during organogenesis produced no developmental effects including teratogenicity in rabbits at dietary levels up to 2.5%.[Siddiqui WH; Teratology 49 (5): 397 (1994) http://toxnet.nlm.nih.gov/cgi-bin/sis/search2/r?dbs+toxline:@term+@DOCNO+DART/TER/94000741] **PEER REVIEWED** </ntox>
<warn>Although no data are available on the use of simethicone during breastfeeding, it is known that simethicone is not absorbed orally. Therefore, it cannot be transferred to breastmilk. It is also used safely in breastfed infants. No special precautions are required.[LacMed; Antifoaming Agents Record on Simethicone (8050-81-5) (LactMed Record 536) revised on September 7, 2013. Available from, as of October 22, 2015: http://toxnet.nlm.nih.gov/cgi-bin/sis/search2/r?dbs+lactmed:@term+@DOCNO+536] **PEER REVIEWED** </warn>
